As for the Investigation Committee chaired by Darrow, its enthusiasm is somewhat untimely. It is likely that the President will order its dissolution. There is no doubt that the committee's report can be used as a tool to attack the government by those who oppose the recovery efforts. Flute Sound Mistaken for Signal: Spanish Train Crash Tragedy - Over Forty Dead and Injured 45

A train crash tragedy occurred in Madrid-Barcelona today, with 20 dead and 25 seriously injured. The cause of the accident is quite bizarre. The train was full of holiday travelers who were in high spirits. One passenger blew a flute as a prank. However, the driver mistakenly thought it was the stationmaster's departure signal. The train departed several minutes before the scheduled departure time, resulting in a head-on collision with another passenger train a few miles away. It can be said that extreme joy turned into sorrow. Ambulances are searching through the wreckage, and it is reported that several more bodies are trapped under the train. (22nd, National Telegram)

Guangdong was previously affected by the Fujian Incident, and the price of paper money was manipulated by unscrupulous merchants, making it very low. Later, the Finance Department, together with the Bank of China, recovered the paper money and destroyed a large amount, and the Bank of China's funds also reached more than 8 million, so it gradually stabilized. Negotiations on the Construction of an Airfield by the Japanese Army in Tianjin - The Japanese Side Ignores Protests - Landowners Sue in Court 94

Tianjin Correspondence: The matter of the Japanese army in Tianjin forcibly occupying land in Balitai, Nankai, Tianjin to build an airfield is still under negotiation as of today. The protest letter sent by the Tianjin Municipal Government to the Japanese Consulate on the 7th of this month will be half a month old by now. The Japanese side has always ignored it, causing our side to feel that the Japanese attitude is unfathomable, and the negotiation feels there is no way to start. On the 17th of this month, the Municipal Government issued a second protest based on the recent investigation report from the Provincial Public Security Bureau, stating all the legal responsibilities of this matter, based on the original land lease of Guangrentang, should be borne by the Japanese side, and reserved the right to claim compensation for damages before the negotiation is resolved. The Provincial Public Security Bureau ordered the police in the Second District to send competent police officers to patrol the area near Balitai in plain clothes every day. The progress of the Japanese construction was reported to the Bureau several times a day, and the Bureau forwarded it to the provincial and municipal governments. As for the airfield's embankment project, more than 130 acres have been completed. No less than 140 or 150 workers are working every day, supervised by several Japanese police officers in shifts, speeding up the work. Ignorant workers, incited by the Japanese, are unusually hostile to Chinese people passing through the area, so many people have been driven away and injured recently. The Central Government has not yet sent any instructions to Tianjin regarding this matter. The Provincial Government is handling this matter in accordance with the wishes of the Beiping Military Branch, temporarily maintaining a calm attitude. All materials have been compiled and submitted to the Central Government, requesting the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to preside over negotiations with Japan. The Municipal Government ordered the Social Affairs Bureau to investigate the original land lease of Guangrentang, why it was transferred from Zhang Shaoqing's name to the Japanese Okura Company. The landowner, Guangrentang, is concerned that if the dispute expands, the company is the original owner, fearing that it will not be understood by the people of the country, so it filed a lawsuit with the Tianjin Local Court yesterday, requesting to summon the original tenant, Zhang Shaoqing, to the court to recover the land property rights and cancel the original contract. Although this move cannot make the Japanese people who enjoy extraterritoriality submit, it is sufficient to prove in the negotiation process that the Japanese side did not obtain the consent of the original owner and started construction on the land. However, silently judging the intention of the Japanese side, no matter how we protest and sue, it cannot prevent their construction from proceeding. (20th)

Tragic Scenes After the Disaster in Northern Sichuan 95

--The Number of Deaths in Guangyuan Alone Exceeds 100,000--

--Epidemics are Prevalent in Xuanhan, Resulting in Even More Deaths--

Chengdu Aviation News: The counties in northern Sichuan that fell into the hands of bandits have now been gradually recovered, but the people have suffered extremely deeply. The number of deaths is more than one million. Even those who are fortunate enough to survive are mostly homeless and displaced in foreign lands. The remaining small portion who have returned to their hometowns are also without clothes, food, cattle, or seeds, and have no way to cultivate the land. At the moment, Liu Xiang, the Sichuan Pacification Supervisor, and Zhang Lan, the Pacification Committee Chairman, have decided on a strategy of suppressing bandits on one hand and pacifying the people on the other. However, the affected counties number 16, and the surviving people number 6 to 7 million. With Sichuan in a state of public and private hardship, where will the huge sum be raised to save these refugees? The future is worrying. The following is an excerpt from the report of the investigation into the disaster areas of Guangyuan and Xuanhan counties dispatched by the official Pacification Committee to see a glimpse of the situation. If the central government does not take measures and the people of the country do not provide assistance, starvation and cold will be more pressing than fire and cattle. Once it breaks loose, the harm will be endless.

Investigation Report on the Bandit Area of Guangyuan 96

The situation of Guangyuan County being ravaged by bandits, according to the investigation reports of Pacification Committee investigators Wan Chucheng and Pang Mingshi, is excerpted as follows: (1) The red bandits engaged in extremely severe massacres wherever they went. According to the Protection Bureau's roster, there were about 17,000 people massacred near Wangcangba. In the four townships, there were more than 100 pits of massacres that could not be investigated, about 7,000 to 8,000 people. More than 2,000 people were killed at Puziling, more than 3,100 people were killed at Mumen, more than 30,000 people were killed at Changchi, more than 800 people were killed at Luojiaba, more than 300 people were killed at Wulangmiao, and more than 900 people were killed in the Pinghe and Daheba areas. A total of more than 230 people were killed at Liulisi and Fenshuiling. More than 170 people were killed at Dahui Houba. Excluding Changchi, which is under the jurisdiction of Nanjiang, the Guang-affiliated districts 5, 6, 7, 8, and 9 had a total of about 32,600 people massacred by the bandits. As for the corpses seen along the way from Guangyuan to Nanjiang, they often numbered in the tens of thousands. Half of those killed in a pit were buried alive. The corpses of women either had children on their backs or infants in their arms. Most of them had wooden sticks inserted into their vaginas. It can be said to be the most tragic sight in the world. In the Yang family's outhouse at Puziling, seventeen or eighteen young children, all two or three years old, were thrown in and drowned while hugging their heads. In the rich households' granaries in Changchi and Mumen, there were many full of human heads. All of this was done by the communists when they were leaving. As for the traces of killing when the bandits first arrived and last year, they have not yet been discovered because the refugees have not returned. I am afraid that once a detailed investigation is conducted, the number of people who died unjustly in this year will be more than the 100,000 mentioned in the previous telegram. (2) About one-twentieth of the civilian houses in each district were burned down, and more than two-tenths were demolished. As for the rest, all the windows and doors were gone, leaving only four walls. (3) The grain in each district had already been completely transported away by the time the bandits retreated. The refugees who remained in the bandit areas still had some grain left to maintain the current situation, but those who fled back to their hometowns had nothing left and could not maintain their livelihood. The people mostly eat tender grass and wild vegetables. There is also an extreme shortage of grain seeds. Many rice paddies have already been leveled, but there are still no grains to sow. The county government is rushing to transport and distribute them. (4) Most of the people in each district who were coerced by the bandits have returned from the front lines of Nanjiang recently because the military and the government have been lenient and not investigating the past. (5) The eastern districts 7, 8, and 9 have been lost for the longest time, and the banditization of various places is also deep. Under the Soviets, there are economic communes, cooperatives, etc. However, the bandits arbitrarily massacred, thus losing the sympathy of the people. (6) Although the sections of Wangcangba, Puziling, Zhenwugong, Miaoerwan, Mumen, Fenshuiling, Nulangmiao, and Malingba in the seven districts have been completely lost, destroyed, and ravaged, fortunately, the winter grain in each place has all been cultivated. To this day, one can still see the bandits' slogans of "Strive for Autumn Harvest, Strive for Cultivation," which shows that the bandits also attached importance to grain cultivation, so there is little wasteland. However, at that time, people were uneasy, and the cultivation was perfunctory. Later, the military and bandits clashed, and irrigation was neglected. When a timely rain fell, the seedlings and grass grew together, which also affected the quantity of the harvest. However, the land for growing tobacco in the past accounted for about one-tenth of the total area. This year, it is all cultivated for grain, compensating for the shift, and may be no different from normal years. However, now that the grain is running out, and there are survivors after the robbery, there is bound to be a sigh of empty pots and broken stoves, etc.

Investigation Report on the Bandit Area of Xuanhan 97

Xuanhan investigators Li Shuyang and Lin Ze investigated the situation in the county as follows: (1) Guandu, Changxi, Huangjinkou, Xiagengkou, Dongshengchang, and other places in Xuanhan were heavily re-occupied by bandits, and many residents were displaced. The livelihood of the people in Dongshengchang is also very dilapidated. However, the most tragic place is Huangjinkou. The grain and rice buried underground by the people have fortunately survived, but the seedlings of peas and rape are almost completely gone. The spring harvest is mostly no more than 10%. Although there are now few troops and refugees left, and the disaster has been eliminated, people are starving to death every day. Hujiacheng, Maoba, Yanshanchang, and parts of Mingguchang, Chixichang, and Maduguan were heavily re-occupied by bandits. Many people were killed, and even more fled. Moreover, the main forces of both sides fought fiercely for more than two months, with corpses all over the fields. The seedlings that were trampled on were innumerable. Not only have many displaced children not returned home, but the local groups have not yet been restored. The remaining waters and mountains are unbearable to look at. In the future, disaster relief measures must be given special emphasis, otherwise it may not be enough to preserve the survivors. Although there is a worry about the lack of food in the various Changs below Aikou, they have been recovered for a long time, and there are no other unexpected losses, so rescue is easier to carry out. (2) The grain seeds in Xuan territory are mostly problematic. At the moment, the personnel handling emergency relief are conducting on-the-spot investigations and providing subsidies to the various towns that are unable to purchase and transport rice seeds, taking into account the situation, from the emergency relief funds they are carrying, so that they can handle it themselves. If it is not enough, they can report back to the county and add more funds. Although there is bound to be a worry about too many monks and too little porridge, in the midst of this financial difficulty, we can only save the emergency situation first. (3) At present, epidemics are prevalent in the various Changs of Xuan territory, especially in the northwest two districts. After inquiring, the number of patients in each Chang is counted in the hundreds, and eight or nine out of ten die without effective treatment. Generally, they die within eight or nine days. After diagnosis, enteritis typhus accounts for eight or nine out of ten, and influenza accounts for two or three out of ten. Treatment is very difficult, especially for enteritis typhus. In the aftermath of this great disaster, money and medicine are both empty, which is deeply worrying. Moreover, the infectious characteristic of enteritis typhus is that the stronger the person, the easier and more severe the illness they suffer, and the faster they die. I think that agricultural labor and hard work all rely on strong men. Now, in the aftermath of the bandit disaster, many strong men have been lost. The work of farming and harvesting mostly falls to the bodies of healthy women. Overcoming this epidemic, what will be the future? Furthermore, from spring to summer, the scorching sun is increasing day by day, and the spread of the infection will have a prairie fire potential. We want to treat but cannot, and we cannot not save. This is what we worry about. We only pray that we appeal to medical and charitable organizations inside and outside the province to send enthusiastic and intelligent doctors with a large number of enteritis typhus preventive injections to inject everywhere. Those who are not sick can be guaranteed not to get sick, and those who are already sick may not be allowed to die, which is a great contribution to preserving the survivors. The investigation shows that the infection is from food and spring water. The duties, etc., have persuaded people to pay attention to cleaning techniques and to set up calamus, Atractylodes lancea, and Asarum roots in drinking water to kill germs. However, in this time of difficulty in making a living, how many can do it, and how many can believe it? Chang is not known. (National News Agency)

Songjiang First District Repairs Roads and Bridges 98

Since the opening of the road for motor vehicles, the water and land transportation in Songcheng has become increasingly convenient. Visitors from outside the area come to Songjiang in droves. Li Zufu, the chief of the first district, believed that Ximen Street, where shops gathered, had a large number of vehicles entering and leaving, and the street pavement was already broken and sunken, or the ditches were blocked, and rainwater accumulated on rainy days, soiling clothes and shoes, which greatly hindered pedestrians. Therefore, it was decided to hire workers day and night to repair the section from Suspension Bridge to Pagoda Bridge. Work was done at night from Suspension Bridge to Long Bridge, and work was done during the day from Long Bridge West to Pagoda Bridge to maintain traffic. Also, because the Huayang Bridge in the eastern suburbs has not yet been leveled, it is quite inconvenient for passengers to get on and off the bus at the bus station. It is also planned to rebuild it. A letter has been sent to Xu Chunbo, the town mayor of the town, inviting local people to gather together to discuss fundraising and planning, and report for approval. Once the bridge is leveled, the bridges in Songcheng can all be used for traffic.

Shao Yuancong of Suzhou Visits Suzhou 99

Shao Yuancong, the Deputy President of the Legislative Yuan, and his wife Zhang Mojun, and Legislative Member Zhang Weihan, arrived in Suzhou from Beijing on the 21st. They hired a boat to go to Mudu for sightseeing and gave a speech at Mudu Elementary School entitled "Don't Forget Saving the Country When Reading." Then they went to Lingyan Mountain to visit the Wang Bei stele. That night, they stayed at Li Yinquan's villa at the foot of Xiaowang Mountain. Yesterday (the 22nd) at 8:00 AM, they went to Shanren Bridge on Qionglong Mountain to follow along. Then they went down the mountain to visit Guangfu. At 4:30 PM, they returned to Mudu and went directly back to the city. It is scheduled to stay for another day today (the 23rd) to visit the scenic spots in the suburbs, such as Tiger Hill outside the city, Liuyuan Garden, Xiyuan Garden, and the Lion Grove in the city.

Kunshan Lake Bandits Rob Bai Shu 100

Yangchenghu in the county has always been a place where bandits haunt. Yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM, shipowners Zhou Zhilin and Zhu Rongxiang loaded 1300 bags of salt from Liuhe and went to Wujin to unload it. Unexpectedly, when they reached Yangchenghu near Bacheng Town, they suddenly encountered two bandit boats. There were more than ten bandits on board, armed with guns, who boarded the ship to rob. When Zhou and others saw this situation, they did not dare to resist. The bandits immediately loaded the salt onto the bandit boat, fired a gun to show off, and set sail. Afterwards, Zhou immediately reported to the Bacheng Public Security Bureau, which sent police to pursue them, but the bandits had already gone far away.

Wuxi Police Officer Brandishes a Weapon and is Taken into Custody 101

Mao Yijun, the director of the Third Branch of the Public Security Bureau, has been working diligently to search and arrest smokers and gamblers for a year since taking office. On the evening of the 11th of last month, Director Mao again dispatched officer Sun Zhongjie to lead the police to arrest 16 gamblers, including Zhu Wangshi, at Zhu Hongda's home under Tatan outside Nanmen. Each was fined, and the bureau issued a receipt for the fine. Recently, a teacher named Hou Zhuoying from a primary school outside Nanmen collected 11 fine slips from this case and had them photographed by a photography studio, pointing out that this fine slip had not been reported. Unexpectedly, officer Sun Zhongjie of the bureau found out about it and went to a photography studio without authorization, daring to bring out five photos of the fine slips taken by Hou and hand them over to a lawyer, personally notifying a lawyer by telephone and urging them to proceed, etc. Director Mao of the branch bureau found out about it, thinking that Sun was unpredictable, so he went to the general bureau to report to the director. Director Chen immediately dispatched Chief Wang Inspector to lead a team of car patrol officers to the third branch bureau at 9:00 AM the day before, summoning officer Sun Zhongjie, employee Pu Jihong, police chief Liu Desheng, office police officer Xu Yi, Shao Liren, Wang Fusheng, etc. to the general bureau together, and searching Sun Zhongjie's bedroom and home once. Later, he ordered to summon the gambler Zhu Wangshi and the head of the map, Pan Hongqi, to the bureau. After Director Chen personally questioned them, he ordered Sun Zhongjie and Xu Yi to be suspended from their duties and taken into custody, and Pu Jihong, Shao Liren, and Wang Fusheng to be released on bail. All the others were ordered to return. Yesterday (the 22nd) at 8:00 AM, Director Chen prepared a document and sent police to transfer Sun Zhongjie, Xu Yi, Pu Jihong, Shao Liren, Wang Fusheng, Liu Desheng, and six others to the local branch of the court for handling. However, it is heard that the director of the branch bureau, Mao Yijun, has also resigned himself.

Chen Diaoyuan

Develops the Longwei Inkstone Stone of Wuyuan

Wuyuan Correspondence: Longwei Mountain is a branch of Furong Ridge, a hundred miles east of the county, connecting Wuxi in the west. The mountains are clear and the waters are beautiful, stretching for more than a hundred miles. The mountain produces inkstone stone, which is the most famous, especially the golden star, jujube core, eyebrow, and brocade patterns are the most valuable. The mountains producing inkstones in that place include Longwei Mountain, Luowen Mountain, Meizi Pit, Jinxing Pit, Biyu Pit, Shuixuan Pit, Shui蕨 Pit, Ye Jiu Pit, Xitou Pit, Lu Pit, Jiyuan Pit (all of the above are in the east of the county), and Lingyan Mountain (in the north of the county), etc., eleven places. However, the stones from each mountain pit have been abandoned since the Northern Song Dynasty, and the years have been lost, and they are all barren. The name of Longwei has long become a historical trace. This time, Chen Diaoyuan led his troops to station in Wuyuan. Seeing that the burial and abandonment of Longwei inkstone stone was a pity, he summoned the county squire Jiang Youbai to the headquarters a few days ago to inquire about the situation of the inkstone stone. According to Jiang's answer, the stone pit has not been opened for many years, and it is full of sand and stones. The location of the stone seedlings is mostly unknown. Only one old man in the village can still remember it. To mine this stone, one must wash away the accumulated sand and stones before one can find and recognize the source of the stone. However, it requires a huge amount of money, which is difficult to start. Chen believed that this stone was so valuable that he decided to take advantage of the fact that this guide was still actively developing it, and invested 1,000 yuan himself, ordering County Magistrate Liu to order the district to start washing away the sand and stones, and then find a way to collect them. After Liu received the order, he was already preparing to proceed. From now on, the Longwei inkstone stone, which has become the Guangling San, will be re-pioneered, and soon it will give a new contribution to the literary and artistic circles. (May 17th)

Page 8

Detailed Hearing of the Liu Zuomin Case 102

Liu Zuomin, the former director of the Second Branch of the Public Security Bureau in this county, and his wife, Wen Rongzhen, were arrested by County Magistrate Yan and sent to the former County Court for questioning because of their resistance to the transfer of power. After the court's prosecutor's office investigated, it was determined that Liu Zuomin and Wen Rongzhen definitely had obstructed official duties, so on the 30th of last month, they filed a public prosecution with the Criminal Court of the same court. It is now known that yesterday (the 20th) was the first day for a public hearing of this case. At 2:00 PM, Judge Liu brought Liu Zuomin and Wen Rongzhen, who were in custody, to the court together. First, he questioned Liu Zuomin, who did not admit to resisting the transfer of power and hiding official seals, etc., and also supplied that Li Shuyun, the wife of Gu Renfa, did not go to Wuxi, etc. Next, Wen Rongzhen was summoned for questioning. Wen testified that she was really wronged in this case. I knew Li Shuyun four or five years ago on a train in Hunan. Liu went to Wuxi to serve as the director of the branch bureau, and I did not tell Li Shuyun that. On the day of the reception, I did not fight with the members from the General Bureau. At that time, because Liu was in the town, I asked the members to come again in a day. Unexpectedly, they wanted me to be responsible for the transfer, and later they put me under surveillance and did not allow me to move freely, etc. By this point, it was already past 5:00 PM. After the interrogation, it was still ordered to be returned to custody and await review.

Nantong Rugao Giant Bribery Case Opens 103

Ru Gao merchants and people Yu Hao, etc., accused the county party committee Lu Peixian, Wu Cishi, Liu Xikun, and obtained a bribe of three thousand two hundred yuan, unsealed the enemy goods, the High Court designated the Nantong Court to hear, the prosecutor concluded the investigation, for the three defendants with intimidation and fraud, to the criminal court filed a public prosecution, the 21st by the Long Shiliang judge public trial, the court ordered the three defendants to bail and await judgment.

Fire Engulfs Eight Homes in Haimen 104

The home of Shi Hongbin in Six District, Sanyang Town, South Fourth Li, caught fire unexpectedly around 4 PM the day before yesterday. The fire originated carelessly in the south end of a west-facing room. A strong southeast wind fanned the flames northward. Despite best efforts to extinguish it, the fire could not be controlled, resulting in the destruction of six brick houses, ten thatched houses, and miscellaneous belongings, belonging to eight households living in the same compound. The estimated loss is around ten thousand yuan.

Important Matters

Compilation of Proposals from the National Financial Conference Regarding Local Finance (Submitted by the Minister for Discussion) 1st: Reorganization of Land Tax 105

Land tax is the oldest tax in our country, but also the one with the most deeply ingrained malpractices. Since the 17th year of the Republic when land tax was assigned to local finance, surcharges have increased daily. Their complexity, harshness, and disorder are difficult to fully understand. The Fourth Plenary Session of this year approved two proposals to reorganize land tax and reduce surcharges. The Executive Yuan has ordered separate implementation. However, the land tax situation is complex and varies from province to province. Implementation standards urgently require joint discussion to facilitate implementation.

A. Implementation of Land Reporting: The Fourth Plenary Session passed the general outline for land reporting, and the Executive Yuan decided on supplementary measures. The following draft articles of the Land Reporting Implementation Regulations are specifically formulated for uniform regulations in implementation, to facilitate discussion and collect opinions from all parties. The following points should be noted: (1) No handling fees will be charged for land reporting; (2) Reporting procedures and forms should be simplified. After reporting, tax rates should be revised to ensure an even burden; (3) Formal tax registers compiled by each county should have uniform regulations; (4) The tax collection system should be improved immediately after reporting; (5) The tax collection system should be improved immediately after reporting.

B. Standards for Reducing Land Tax Surcharges: The severity of land tax surcharges varies from province to province and county to county, in some cases exceeding ten times the principal tax. The ways to effectively reduce or eliminate them should be determined on a case-by-case basis when reviewing budgets, and tax rates should be revised after land reporting to achieve a comprehensive solution. The following articles are proposed as restrictions before land tax is fully reorganized: (1) Land tax surcharges should not exceed the total amount of the principal tax. In areas where the principal tax rate is originally low, the combined principal and surcharges should not exceed 1% of the land value; (2) Regardless of whether land tax surcharges already exceed the principal tax, provinces and counties are prohibited from increasing them for any urgent needs or under any pretext starting this year; (3) Temporary mu (unit of area) levies and apportionments in counties, districts, townships, and towns should be strictly prohibited. If expenses are incurred per mu for the public interest of the district, township, or town, the province should formulate regulations for stricter restrictions; (4) Surcharges collected for a fixed term or for a specific purpose that no longer exists should be abolished immediately and not used for other purposes or continue to be collected.

2nd: Improving the Local Tax System

Since the promulgation of the National and Local Revenue and Expenditure Standards in the 17th year of the Republic, all items previously under the central government, such as deed tax and broker tax, were assigned to local governments. After the central government implemented the abolition of likin (internal transit tax) in the 20th year of the Republic, the business tax law was promulgated, and provinces and cities began implementing business tax. Local governments now have various taxes, and their scope is expanding daily. It is urgent to carry out rectification to increase financial resources. Increasing regular tax revenue must precede the easy abolition of harsh and miscellaneous taxes. The following is a breakdown of the points that should be rectified for the existing local regular taxes and the unification of tax collection agencies for discussion.

A. Business Tax: Since the implementation of business tax, more than two years have passed. Apart from a few provinces that have achieved some results, most have encountered numerous obstacles and have failed to achieve the expected results. Based on the experience of the past two years, it is believed that several aspects of the collection method need to be improved: (1) Investigation Certificates Should Be Changed to Tax Certificates. Article 3 of the Business Tax Law originally stipulated that merchants should apply for a business tax investigation certificate. However, this article does not clearly define the items to be listed on the investigation certificate. Tax collection agencies in various provinces and cities issue investigation certificates based on the matters in Articles 3, 1-4, that merchants must follow when applying. The amount of tax payable by business operators is not specified in the certificate. Furthermore, the name "investigation certificate" is not very suitable. It is proposed to issue business tax certificates in the form of licenses, without charging any fees, and require merchants to display them, using the tax certificate as the basis for collecting taxes. The tax certificate should specify the following: 1. Business type and store name; 2. Business operator's name, place of origin, and residence; 3. Taxable standard and tax rate; 4. Annual tax payable; 5. Average tax payable per period. The tax certificate should be renewed annually without collecting any fees. (2) Limits on Tax Rate Grading: Currently, provinces and cities use both capital and turnover as taxable standards. No province or city uses net income as the standard. The number of grades into which the tax rate is divided is often too detailed, causing inconvenience to both taxpayers and tax collectors. It is proposed to divide the tax rate into three grades for those taxed on turnover and four grades for those taxed on capital. A grading table is attached separately. (3) Limits on Industry Classification: Business tax collection is based on industry. The number of industry types currently divided in various provinces and cities is too many and inconsistent. Uniform regulations are urgently needed for sorting. The level of the tax rate is related to the nature of the industry, and it is even more necessary to have separate standards. An industry classification table and an industry classification tax standard table are attached separately. (4) No Tax Collection on Goods: Business tax should be collected on employment in principle, not on goods as the unit of collection. Collection from the sale and manufacture of goods should be limited to those with a fixed place of business or manufacturing site. Business tax similar to likin should not be collected on goods. (5) Strict Adherence to Tax Collection Restrictions: The standards for business tax rates are clearly stipulated in Article 4 of the Business Tax Law. Article 5 stipulates that businesses with a turnover of less than 1,000 yuan or a capital of less than 500 yuan should be exempt from tax. It is necessary to strictly adhere to this provision so that small businesses can receive the practical benefits of tax law protection.

B. Broker Tax: The problems with broker tax in various provinces and cities are mostly due to the inconsistent taxable standards, the absence of fixed restrictions on the commission rate, and the imperfect collection system. According to Article 10 of the Business Tax Law, there is a provision to temporarily change to business tax according to the original tax rate. The broker tax should be reorganized to gradually bring it into the legal scope of business tax, to eliminate harassment. The following points should be reorganized: (1) Limit Brokerage Firms: Brokerage firms should have fixed trading posts in counties, cities, towns, and market trading locations, regardless of whether they are operating in the short or long term. They are not allowed to set up card checkpoints or intercept and collect commissions along the road in trading markets. (2) Determine the Responsibilities of Brokerage Firms: Brokerage firms are intermediaries for the sale of goods. They should be responsible to the buyer for the completeness of the goods sold, and responsible to the seller for compensating the price of the goods sold. They should not dispatch brokers to solicit customers outside the port before the goods arrive. They should not force customers who directly buy or sell goods to consign the goods through brokerage firms. They should not prevent customers who have already arrived at the port from consigning the goods through other firms. (3) Restrict Brokerage Commissions: The brokerage commission rates vary greatly from province to province, ranging from about 1% to 5%. Now that agriculture and commerce are in difficulty and prices are falling, restrictions should be imposed. It is proposed to uniformly limit the maximum to 3%, with provinces and cities considering local trading conditions and determining the restrictions accordingly. (4) Brokerage Business Tax: The standard for brokerage taxation should be based on transaction or sales volume. The standards for brokerage taxation vary from province to province, with some based on sales volume and others on brokerage commissions. As a result, the tax rate borne by brokers is often disproportionately high or low. It should be stipulated that the annual or quarterly business tax payable by brokerage firms (i.e., regular tax) should be based on the total sales volume introduced by them. (5) Abolish Itinerant Brokers: The nature of brokerage firms varies from province to province. Some brokers are itinerant, operating in the open air. Although they also collect commissions after obtaining permits, they do not have fixed trading posts. They mostly collect commissions directly on the goods, which is illegal and disruptive, and creates many malpractices. The tax revenue does not compensate for the losses. These brokers should be abolished uniformly. (6) Strictly Correct Improper Collection Methods: Provinces and cities should not have broker tax that is disguised as a commodity tax. Brokerage firms that have been contracted by merchants through bidding or entrusted by government agencies to collect taxes should only be allowed to do so for the period specified in the contract. All such arrangements should be abolished after the contract expires, and there should be no more terms such as contract collection, special collection, or delegated collection, to eliminate harassment.

C. Deed Tax: Deed tax rates vary from province to province. In addition to the principal tax, there are many surcharges, which leads to more and more people hiding prices and evading taxes, which in turn affects the principal tax. In addition, transfer and tax deeds are completely separate matters. Property transfer is avoided due to concealing tax payment, which also avoids transfer tax. Grain pillars (tax payment receipts) lack evidence, and malpractices are even deeper. The following are several ways to reorganize: (1) The deed tax rate is tentatively set at no more than 6% for sales deeds and no more than 3% for mortgage deeds; (2) Deed tax surcharges should not exceed half of the principal tax; (3) Transfer tax should be processed at the same time as deed tax. Tax payment and transfer should be processed at the same time; (4) Uniform deed forms should be formulated. Transfer and the amount of principal tax payable should be stated in the deed. All transfer stamps can be abolished.

D. Unification of Collection Agencies: Today, local tax collection agencies are too complicated, with approximately four types: (1) Business tax bureaus specifically for collecting business tax; (2) County government finance bureaus for collecting land tax and other provincial and county taxes; (3) County government finance sections for collecting provincial and county taxes in counties without finance bureaus; (4) Bureaus and offices of other departments for collecting special funds (such as the Slaughtering and Brokerage Tax Collection Office in various counties contracted by Jiangsu Education Fund Management Office. In other provinces, the county finance bureau or county finance section is entrusted to collect the tax on their behalf). Among these four types of collection agencies, only the business tax bureau has a clear and specific responsibility and can be fully responsible to the finance department. The rest, due to different affiliations, lead to various malpractices such as shirking responsibility and encroachment. Contractors are even more difficult to supervise and direct. If we want to establish the foundation of local finance, we should unify the local tax collection agencies. All business tax, broker tax, pawn tax, slaughtering tax, and special funds originally collected by various departments should be collected uniformly by the local tax bureaus established by the finance department in each county. Only in this way can the improvement of the tax system, the audit of collection, and the training of tax collectors begin. Furthermore, the people will only know that there is one tax payment agency, and they will not be deceived by tax officials. The method of unification is as follows: (1) In order to unify the collection of local taxes, each province should establish a local tax bureau in each county. All business tax, broker tax, pawn tax, slaughtering tax, and other provincial and county taxes and fees should be collected and remitted by the bureau; (2) Each county's local tax bureau is under the command and supervision of the finance department. The organizational regulations are determined by each province; (3) After the establishment of the local tax bureau, all previous methods such as bidding, contracting, and entrusting collection should be abolished.

3rd: Abolishing Harsh Taxes and Miscellaneous Fees

Since the first National Financial Conference in the 17th year of the Republic resolved to divide national and local revenue and expenditure standards and promulgate it, local taxation should be based on guidelines and follow a proper path. However, local taxes and fees have become increasingly burdensome, and calls for reform are endless. The reason for this is that at the beginning of the reform, there were omissions. Some items were only listed but never implemented (such as the surcharges on income tax, which is a nominal item). Some items were prepared but then abolished (such as the inland fishing tax, which was explicitly exempted). Some new sources of revenue were slow to develop or failed to achieve results (such as the business tax, which was originally a major source of local revenue, but was not successively implemented by provinces and cities until after the abolition of likin in the 20th year of the Republic, and the amount collected was not very strong). Some should have revised the tax system according to law, but they have not been revised or have become even worse (such as local broker tax). The Business Tax Law stipulates that business tax should be temporarily changed according to the original tax rate. However, various provinces and cities have not revised it or have changed it to contracted collection, delegated collection, and taxation on goods. Because local governments' expenditures have gradually increased and the foundation of revenue has not been consolidated, they have been eager to choose any method to meet the needs of their operations and have independently established items and taken money from the people. As a result, harsh taxes and miscellaneous fees have come one after another, harming businesses and disturbing the people. To reorganize local taxes and fees, it is necessary to define the types and scope to clarify the system, and it is even more necessary to clearly define the collection procedures to show uniformity. Based on current laws and regulations and the current tax system in various provinces and cities, the types and scope of local taxes and fees are defined as follows:

(1) Land Tax Category: 1. Land tax (including current land tax, grain tribute, rent tax, salt tax, fishing tax, reed tax, etc.); 2. Legal land tax surcharges (not exceeding the principal tax, and in areas with low principal tax rates, the combined principal and surcharges should not exceed 1% of the land value); 3. Land value tax collected in accordance with the Land Law; 4. House tax or shop tax (collected according to the property or rental value of the house); 5. Deed tax; 6. Deed tax surcharges.

(2) Business Tax Category: 1. Business tax collected in accordance with the Business Tax Law; 2. Broker tax, pawn tax, slaughtering tax, etc., that should be changed in accordance with the Business Tax Law; 3. Business tax that should be banned in accordance with the law (such as vehicle tax, boat tax, advertising tax, etc.).

(3) Conduct Tax: 1. Collected directly (such as divination, astrology, etc.); 2. Collected indirectly (such as banquet tax for restaurants, entertainment tax for theaters, etc.).

(4) Public Welfare Tax Category: 1. Fees collected from beneficiaries and vehicles or other users for improving or repairing all land and water conservancy projects (such as road construction tax, dike construction tax, water conservancy tax, pier tax, warehouse tax, port affairs tax); 2. Fees collected from the people by local governments or autonomous organizations for public welfare or health undertakings, in accordance with legal procedures (such as health tax, street light tax).

(5) Handling Fee Category: 1. Paper prices for official documents collected by local governments at all levels in accordance with the law; 2. Deed prices collected by local governments at all levels in accordance with the law; 3. Various fines collected by local governments at all levels in accordance with the law; 4. Verification fees, handling fees, and registration fees collected by local governments at all levels in accordance with the law.

Since the above-mentioned scope of taxes and fees collected locally has been determined, the collection procedures should be specified in detail to achieve the effect of effective reorganization, and local governments can have a basis for avoiding difficulties. The following points should be specified first in the collection procedure: (1) Provinces and cities that collect taxes and fees legally listed in this proposal and that began collecting before the State Council promulgated the National and Local Revenue and Expenditure Standards in November of the 17th year of the Republic should list the name, purpose, tax rate, estimated collection amount, and collection month of the taxes and fees in a special report to the Ministry; (2) Provinces and cities that collect taxes and fees listed in this proposal but that have not been implemented in accordance with current laws or regulations and that began collecting after the State Council promulgated the National and Local Revenue and Expenditure Standards in November of the 17th year of the Republic should list the name, purpose, tax rate, estimated collection amount, and collection month of the taxes and fees in a special report to the Ministry and forward it to the Legislative Yuan for review; (3) Starting from the 23rd year of the Republic, provinces and cities shall not collect any taxes and fees outside the scope stipulated in this proposal without legislative procedures; (4) Provinces and cities shall not change the original tax items or tax rates without the provisions of laws or regulations; (5) If the collection of taxes and fees or the increase or decrease of tax items by provinces and cities conflicts with the provisions of laws or regulations, the Ministry of Finance may stop or revoke them at any time; (6) Local governments at all levels may collect the fees listed in the handling fee category, but they must collect them in accordance with the provisions of current laws or regulations and report them to the superior government or the competent department for record.

Since there are detailed decisions on the scope and procedures for the collection of local taxes and fees, taxes and fees that exceed the legal tax rate range or that exceed the scope stipulated in this proposal should be regarded as harsh and miscellaneous taxes and abolished. The types are as follows: (1) Surcharges on central taxes; (2) Taxes and fees that harm social public interests; (3) Taxes and fees that harm the source of central revenue; (4) Duplicate taxes that are the same as current taxes; (5) Taxes and fees that obstruct transportation and are collected on the passage of goods or vehicles; (6) Taxes that unfairly tax the import of local goods for the benefit of one locality; (7) Taxes and fees collected on the production or sale of goods; (8) Surcharges on current business tax; (9) All taxes and fees that harm the livelihood of the common people. All of the above should be abolished in stages from July 1, 23rd year of the Republic to the end of December 23rd year of the Republic. Those who have not been collected should not arbitrarily start them under any pretext or in any name, so that the people's suffering can be relieved as soon as possible, the foundation of local finance can be established, and the national economy and people's livelihood can be relied upon.

4th: Determining Local Budgets

To reorganize finances, the first step is to determine the budget. The above-mentioned matters of reorganizing land tax, improving tax administration, and abolishing harsh taxes and miscellaneous fees are all related to the budget. How should local budgets at all levels be prepared and executed to gradually bring local finance onto the right track and alleviate the people's difficulties? The problem is very complicated. Now, we will choose several points that are more important and more urgently needed to provide for discussion.

A. Division of Local Revenue and Expenditure between Provinces and Counties/Cities: When provinces and county/city governments prepare local budgets, they must allocate and control resources within their respective scopes. Therefore, it is necessary to establish specific standards for how provinces and counties/cities divide revenue and expenditure. However, the situations in various provinces are different. The standards for this division should be formulated by the provincial governments themselves and submitted to the central government for approval and implementation. However, the following points must be noted when formulating the standards: (1) Regarding the revenue and expenditure of counties/cities, the revenue and expenditure originally belonging to the counties/cities and their districts, townships, and towns should be combined into one. There should be no further division below the county/city level, so that the finances of the county/city and its districts, townships, and towns are unified; (2) Regarding the division of tax revenue, the attribution should be based on the type of tax, not on the distinction between principal tax and surtax. For major taxes that cannot be completely attributed to the province or county/city, they should be distributed according to percentages, so that the finances of the province and county/city each have a relatively stable foundation; (3) Regarding the division of expenditure, it should be based on the affiliation of its agencies and the purpose of its business facilities, so that the rights and obligations of the people in various places are reasonably equal; (4) After the division of tax revenue between the province and the county/city, they should not add surcharges to each other, so as to reorganize themselves; (5) After the division of expenditure between the province and the county/city, they must still assist each other when necessary to achieve balanced development.

B. Key Points for Formulating Regulations for Local Budgets of Counties/Cities: How local budgets of counties/cities should be handled is not specified in the current central budget regulations. Each province should formulate separate regulations for compliance. However, the following points should be noted in the formulated measures: (1) When county/city governments prepare and review local budgets, they must allow legal entities and citizens to participate and express their opinions to show financial transparency. The supervision of the budget must be carried out by agencies other than the administrative agencies to prevent malpractices. The Finance Committee established under the Regulations for Reorganizing Local Finances of Counties in the Bandit Suppression Area promulgated by the Bandit Suppression Headquarters of the three provinces of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui has the above-mentioned meaning and is very worthy of learning from; (2) All revenue and expenditure of local public ownership, regardless of its source or purpose, must be included in its budget to show its entire financial situation; (3) The budget items should be as clear as possible so that the general public can easily understand them; (4) The budget preparation and review procedures should be as simple as possible, using meetings and inspections to eliminate barriers, reduce document transfers, and save time; (5) The budget announcement date must be at least one month before the start of the year to prepare for implementation; (6) The execution of the budget and the supplementary budget must have strict regulations to prevent the abuse of harsh levies.

C. Matters to be Noted by Local Governments at All Levels in the Preparation of Budgets during the Period of Reorganization of Local Finances: (1) Local budgets at all levels should be based on revenue and expenditure to make them easy to establish and implement effectively; (2) Expenditure should be tightened as much as possible, and appropriate ratios should be set for administrative expenses and business expenses to reduce consumption and promote production; (3) Tax revenue should be listed as regular revenue, and illegal taxes and surcharges exceeding the quota can only be listed as temporary revenue until they are reduced to gain the people's understanding and tolerance; (4) The central and local finances are currently facing difficulties. Local budgets at all levels must find ways to increase revenue and reduce expenditure to adapt to the situation. They should not request subsidies from superior governments unless they encounter incidents or special facilities; (5) When the provincial and municipal local budgets are sent to the Directorate-General of Budget, Accounting and Statistics, a copy should be sent to the Ministry of Finance. After the provincial government approves the county/city local budgets, the provincial government should send a copy to the Ministry of Finance for reference.

First Proposal Group: Fujian Provincial Department of Finance 112

Proposal to Implement the Reduction of Surtaxes on Field Taxes to Alleviate the People's Suffering in Accordance with the Ministry of Finance's Measures for Reorganizing Field Taxes Surtaxes.

(Reasoning) Upon investigation, the surtaxes on field taxes in various counties of Fujian Province are numerous and complex. Those belonging to the provincial treasury include a 10% surcharge for grain donation, ticket fees, a 20% collection fee, and a highway fee, totaling four types. Those belonging to the local governments include a county police surtax, education fee, new education fee, self-government fee, group fee, and other local surtaxes, totaling six types. Among these, the 10% surcharge for grain donation, ticket fees, 20% collection fee, highway fee, county police surtax, education fee, and new education fee are common to all counties in the province. However, approximately twenty counties also have self-government fees, group fees, and other local surtaxes. Among the three, the group fee is the heaviest. The method of collection is also very uneven. In terms of surtaxes on field taxes, the higher ones reach three yuan per tael, which far exceeds the amount of the principal tax. The lower ones reach one yuan, which is equivalent to half of the principal tax. If all counties uniformly collect this tax, based on the calculation of 50% of the province's grain quota, it would reach over 1.5 million yuan. No policy is more harmful to the people than this. Now, for the sake of addressing the root cause and ensuring clarity, the following reduction measures are proposed:

(Measures) 1. The Department of Finance shall draft a survey form for surtaxes on field taxes and issue it to all counties with a deadline for response. It shall investigate and ascertain the types of surtaxes existing in each county in addition to the principal tax on land and population, as well as their tax rates, amounts, and uses, in order to make separate approvals or exemptions based on this information. 2. If the surtax on field taxes exceeds the principal tax, regardless of the reason, it should be resolutely reduced. 3. After the surtaxes on field taxes reported by each county have been reviewed and approved, they shall be submitted to the provincial government for announcement. Hereafter, no expenditure, regardless of its nature, may be requested from the surtaxes on field taxes, nor may the cancelled surtaxes be used for other purposes. 4. If any county collects surtaxes on field taxes without authorization after approval, it shall be punished as privately collecting taxes. 5. The reduction procedure shall follow Article 4 of the measures promulgated by the Ministry, with administrative expenses being given priority, followed by project expenses. 6. After the surtaxes on field taxes have been reduced, the county government shall convene a meeting of various community organizations, gentry, and merchants to comprehensively plan for any shortfalls, or seek other sources of funding, pending the increase in the grain quota resulting from the re-measurement of fields to compensate for the shortfall. The above proposals are submitted for public deliberation to determine their appropriateness.

First Group (Proposer: Jiangxi Provincial Department of Finance) 113

Proposal to Issue Land Reorganization Public Bonds to Conduct Field Measurement to Implement Fundamental Solutions for Reorganizing Field Taxes.

(Reasoning) Regarding the collection of taxes, nothing is more important than simple procedures, reliable tax sources, and fair burdens. The reorganization of field taxes cannot deviate from these principles. However, due to the chaotic nature of tax regulations, the mixture of population and grain levies, the loss of maps and registers, and the concealment of names in our country's field tax system, clerks and insiders engage in fraud, powerful individuals rely on their influence to resist payment, and taxes are arbitrarily levied and fraudulently transferred, resulting in numerous malpractices. To speak of reorganization, the only fundamental solution lies in "assessing grain based on land" and converting to a land value tax. However, implementing a land value tax must begin with measuring fields, which cannot be accomplished in a short period of time. It is necessary to temporarily adopt a "assessing grain based on households" as a temporary measure. Regarding the situation in Jiangxi, with the exception of counties such as Gao'an and Jing'an, which have well-organized volunteer drawing systems and can collect the full amount of taxes each year, most other counties collect only about 70-80% at most, and only 20-30% at least. The reason for this is that the grain registers contain many household names that are not easy to verify. Jian Tao's method of organizing volunteer drawing is a relatively effective way of assessing grain based on households. Therefore, by adopting the successful cases of volunteer drawing in Gao'an and Jing'an, and incorporating new regulations, a general rule for volunteer drawing has been drafted, and a procedure for implementation has been established. The main points include clarifying the names of grain households, compiling registers for collection, stipulating the responsibilities of drawing heads and township leaders, and limiting the period for clearing the drawing and verifying its accuracy. Since the issuance of these rules in the autumn of the year before last, only about twenty counties have reported their completion, due to local unrest and deeply ingrained habits. Even if it were implemented throughout the province, it would only be possible to hold the drawing heads and township leaders accountable for the names of the grain households. In terms of collection, it may gradually become effective, but the problems of having land without grain and having grain without land would still not be completely eliminated, which is not consistent with the goal of reorganizing field taxes. Therefore, assessing grain based on households is only a temporary measure. (Measures) The fundamental solution is to convert to a land value tax, because the purpose of the land value tax is to ensure that those who have land must have grain, and those who have grain must have land. In other words, the grain follows the land, and the land and grain are combined. Therefore, to adopt this tax system, it is necessary to first measure the fields and go through procedures such as investigation, valuation, and registration before it can be implemented. In July of the twenty-first year, Jiangxi entrusted the Aerial Survey Jiangxi Branch of the General Bureau of Land Surveying of the General Staff Headquarters to first conduct aerial surveys in Nanchang as a pilot project. By January of the twenty-third year, 8,615 original field maps had been produced. The work of investigation, calculation, mapping, and registration was handled by the Jiangxi Provincial Land Reorganization Office. The various tasks are nearing completion. Once the land value is assessed, land registration will be carried out to serve as the basis for abolishing the population and land tax and converting to a land value tax. However, the expenses for the aerial survey in Nanchang County and various tasks were shared by the eight counties of Nanchang, Xinjian, Fengcheng, Qingjiang, Jinxian, Anyi, Xingan, and Gao'an according to the amount of population and land tax. A surveying fee of 400,000 yuan was borrowed. It is now planned to continue using aerial surveys to produce original field maps for the ten counties of Xinjian, Fengcheng, Qingjiang, Jinxian, Anyi, Xingan, Gao'an, Linchuan, Jinxi, and Dongxiang. Considering the excessive cost in Nanchang, triangulation will not be used, and only longitudinal and transverse triangulation chains will be implemented for correction. The deadline for completion is two years. All tasks of investigation, calculation, mapping, registration, valuation, and registration will be carried out in sequence, and the deadline is also set at two years. The total cost is estimated to be over 2.22 million yuan. When the ten counties have achieved considerable results, the plan will be extended to the remaining seventy counties, which will require approximately 8.09 million yuan for aerial surveying and various tasks. The total cost will be over 10.31 million yuan. If this huge amount of funding is still borrowed and collected from the counties along with the grain tax, it would be difficult for the people to bear, considering Jiangxi's years of banditry and the bankruptcy of the rural economy. It should be centrally planned by the government to alleviate the burden on the people and achieve success. It is found that other provinces' land reorganization projects, except for Jiangsu Province, which collects surveying fees along with the grain tax and has sufficient funds for application, are generally hampered by a lack of funds and cannot progress. The surveying of fields and the implementation of various tasks are fundamental to the reorganization of field taxes. Although the land reorganization plan is approved by the Ministry of Interior, it is proposed that the Department centrally plan and manage the funding aspect. According to the needs of each province, the revenue from surveying and measuring fees will be used as a fund to issue land reorganization public bonds. The funds raised will be deposited in banks, or the banks will raise funds to underwrite the bonds using the public bonds as collateral, and allocate them as needed. The land administration agencies of each province will use these funds, and the Department will appoint accounting specialists to manage them. The surveying and measuring fees collected by each province should be deposited in banks for timely disbursement of the principal and interest of the public bonds, or for repayment of the underwriting funds. With funding in place, success can be achieved on schedule, and this can be used as the basis for promoting the land value tax, so that it conforms to the principles of simple procedures, reliable tax sources, and fair burdens. The most difficult to solve field tax problem in our country can also be easily resolved. It is submitted for public deliberation whether the reasons for proposing the issuance of land reorganization public bonds to provide sufficient funding for surveying fields are appropriate.

Page 9

The Panchen Lama Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday Afternoon Thousands of People Welcome Him, Showing the Spirit of Unity Among the Five Races Two Decorated Arches are Erected, and Numerous Guards are Stationed Along the Way The Diplomatic Building is Decorated in Yellow Stays in Shanghai for a Week, Then Goes to the Capital and Returns to Tibet to Govern 114

National Government Committee Member Panchen Lama, the Protector of the Country, has completed the Kalachakra initiation he presided over in Hangzhou. At the invitation of Mayor Wu and various circles, he arrived in Shanghai by special train from Hangzhou yesterday afternoon. At 4:50 PM, he arrived at the South Station and proceeded directly to the Diplomatic Building residence at Maple Forest Bridge to rest. Mayor Wu Tiecheng, Wang Yiting, Wang Xiaolai, Wu Guangxin, and other representatives from various circles all went to the station to greet him, making it a grand occasion. The Panchen Lama came south to Hangzhou in 1924 and visited Shanghai along the way. This is his second time. He is scheduled to stay for a week, then go to the capital to seek instructions from the central government, and then return to Tibet to preside over the major affairs of the country. Details are recorded below.

The Panchen Lama arrived at the South Station yesterday. A decorated arch with the words "Welcome Panchen Lama to Shanghai" was erected at the entrance and exit of the South Station. Inside the station, yellow silk ribbons and彩球 were hung everywhere. The passageway was covered with yellow cloth. The Security Department specially dispatched two battalions of security guards around the station to set up sentries and provide security. The route from the South Station to the Diplomatic Building was from the South Railway Station, via Station Front Road, Guohuo Road, Difangting Road, Daxing Street, Wenlin Road, Fangxie Road, Xieqiao, turning to Manufacturing Bureau Road, Xietu Road, Xiaomuqiao Road, and Municipal Government Road to reach the Diplomatic Building. He An's team cooperated with the police to set up posts along the way. A police squad was specially stationed in front of the Diplomatic Building, providing tight security.

After arriving at the Diplomatic Building, the Panchen Lama rested briefly and then received reporters from Chinese and foreign newspapers in the city to give a speech, which was translated by his secretary-general, Liu Jianqiu. He planned to stay for a week to take the opportunity to tour the city and visit various construction projects, and then go to the capital. As for whether he would go to Jiangxi to meet with Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, he would decide after arriving in the capital.

Returning to Tibet to Govern 124

The reporter then asked when he would return to Tibet to preside over the major affairs of Tibet. He replied that he had been away from Tibet for a long time. Since the passing of the Dalai Lama, there was no one to preside over Tibetan affairs, so he was eager to return to Tibet. He had previously sent representatives, including Anqin, to Tibet, who had now returned to Beijing. He knew that the Tibetan people were eager for him to return to Tibet soon, and there were many letters and telegrams urging him to return. Therefore, after seeking instructions from the central government in Beijing, he would return to Tibet to preside over the government. As for the route back to Tibet, whether it would be via India or Qinghai, it had not yet been decided. The Panchen Lama believed that the Kangzang dispute was a local matter and not the entire Kangzang issue, and it would not escalate.

Efforts in Construction 125

The reporter then asked how the Lama would bridge the gap between the central government and Tibet and enhance unity after returning to Tibet to preside over the government. He replied that he had come south in the early years of the Republic and had stayed in Beijing, Ping, Shanghai, Hangzhou, and other places. He also had a general understanding of the construction projects in various places. After returning to Tibet this time, he would make efforts in various construction projects. He was determined to uphold the spirit of unity among the five races. After returning to Tibet, he would also promote the virtues and intentions of the central government so that the Tibetan people could fully understand the true meaning of the Three Principles of the People. The entourage he brought with him was able to study the

Kalachakra Initiation 128

Finally, regarding the Kalachakra initiation, he said that it was initiated by lay Buddhists in Beijing, Shanghai, and Hangzhou as a purely religious expression, with the purpose of praying for national prosperity, peace, and world peace. He was happy to preside over it, and now it was completed. When the Panchen Lama spoke, his attitude was extremely sincere. After each sentence, he silently recited sutras with his eyes closed, and his eyes were sharp and piercing, showing that he was a man of extraordinary wisdom.

Two Railways Continue to Repay Debts The Beijing-Shanghai Railway Allocates the 57th Installment of Interest The Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Allocates the 32nd Installment of Principal and Interest 134

Totaling More Than 1.79 Million Yuan

According to the Central News Agency, the two railway bureaus have continued to pay the 57th installment of interest on the Beijing-Shanghai Railway loan and the 32nd installment of principal and interest on the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway loan. The Accounting Office converted the amounts into British pounds and remitted them to London through HSBC. The two amounts totaled more than 1.79 million yuan. Of this amount, 300,000 yuan was allocated by the Ministry of Railways, and the remainder was raised by the bureaus themselves. Details are as follows:

Beijing-Shanghai Interest 135

The Beijing-Shanghai Railway was due to pay the 57th installment of interest on the loan from the British and Chinese Corporation, due on November 17 of the 21st year, amounting to £69,600, plus a bank commission of £174, totaling £69,774. The bureau collected the full amount and instructed the Accounting Office to settle the exchange rate with Lao Zhongyong Foreign Firm in two parts: (1) On April 24 of this year, £25,000 was settled at a rate of one shilling and three and three-quarter pence per yuan; (2) On May 18 of this year, £44,774 was settled at a rate of one shilling and three and seven-sixteenth pence per yuan. The above two parts totaled 1,077,034 yuan in national currency, which was fully allocated to HSBC on May 18 for remittance to London.

Shanghai-Hangzhou Principal and Interest 136

The Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway was due to pay the British and Chinese Corporation the 32nd installment of principal on the loan, due on May 18 of this year, including bank commission, totaling £37,593 and 15 shillings, plus the interest on this installment, including bank commission, totaling £9,398 and 8 shillings and 9 pence. Of this amount, the net amount to be allocated was £46,491 and 8 shillings and 11 pence, after deducting £406 and 5 shillings remaining from the £18,500 remitted to London on April 3 of this year, and £94 and 9 shillings and 10 pence for the half-percent interest on the advance loan for the 27th and 28th installments given by the British and Chinese Corporation last year. The Accounting Office settled the exchange rate with Lao Zhongyong Foreign Firm in two installments: (1) On April 24, £23,500 was settled at a rate of one shilling and three and three-quarter pence per yuan; (3) On May 18, £22,991 and 8 shillings and 11 pence were settled at a rate of one shilling and three and seven-sixteenth pence per yuan. The two parts totaled 715,533 yuan and 1 jiao in national currency, which was fully allocated to HSBC on May 18 for remittance to London.

Organization of a Great Construction Bank Corporation 137

Capital Stock of 10 Million Yuan

Has Been Approved by All Parties

A Prelude to the Development of the Northwest

According to the Shenshi News Agency, after Mr. Song Ziwen's return from his inspection tour, he believes that the Northwest, with its vast territory, is the only lifeline of the Chinese nation and that it is necessary to actively develop it. He is even more enthusiastic about the plan for the Construction Bank Corporation. A reporter from the Shenshi News Agency has made a special recording of the recent preparatory situation of the company, as follows:

Submitting to the Ministry for Registration 138

The initiators of the Construction Bank Corporation, including Song Ziwen, Li Shizeng, Kong Xiangxi, Bei Songsun, Shao Lizi, Yang Huchen, Tang Shoumin, Chen Guangfu, etc., have translated the previously drafted company articles of association, originally in English, into Chinese, and submitted them to the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry for registration in accordance with the Company Law and the Company Law Implementation Regulations, requesting the issuance of a business license. As soon as the license is issued, they can publicly advertise for subscriptions, convene a shareholders' meeting, elect officers, and begin operations. It is heard that the registration fee of more than 600 yuan has been remitted to the Ministry and will be approved soon.

Determination of Share Subscriptions 139

The capital stock of the Construction Bank Corporation is fixed at 10 million yuan. The full amount was subscribed by the initiators before Mr. Song's trip to the Northwest. However, in recent weeks, there have been some changes in the previously subscribed shares. The exact amount has been determined again recently. According to inquiries from various sources by the reporter, the exact amounts are as follows: Bank of China, 2 million yuan; Communications Bank, 1.5 million yuan; China Industrial Corporation, 500,000 yuan; Jin Cheng Bank and Zhongnan Bank, 250,000 yuan each; Zhejiang Industrial Bank, Shanghai Commercial & Savings Bank, Continental Bank, Sze Ming Bank, Bank of Communications, and the Gold Exchange and Securities Exchange, 150,000 yuan each; Juxingcheng, Jiangzhe Bank, and Donglai Bank, 100,000 yuan each. Yesterday, Bei Songsun, manager of the Bank of China, told a reporter from the Shenshi News Agency that the 2 million yuan subscribed by the Bank of China is for the purpose of recruitment and will not necessarily be Bank of China shares in the future.

Business Policy 140

The Construction Bank Corporation is entirely for investment in the Northwest and is the overall authority for design, credit, investigation, and management for those investing in Northwest projects. Investment projects are very broad, including water conservancy, sanitation, animal husbandry, reclamation, and mining. The capital required is very large and is not limited to just 10 million yuan. In the future, if a project is to be developed in the Northwest and the entire plan requires capital of tens of millions of yuan, the bank can temporarily raise capital from various parties, design and operate the project. Investors can rest assured with the organization of this trust institution, without having to manage it themselves. This type of organization is used for domestic and foreign investment in European and American countries. It is very common and effective. Our country is 生 落後, and there is 談 唔到 about foreign investment. There is also no organized structure for domestic investment. The Construction Bank Corporation planned by Mr. Song will pioneer large-scale industrial operations in our country.

American Chamber of Commerce of California Vice President Peng De's Impressions of China: All Construction Affairs Must Not Adhere to Old Ways 142

According to the Continental Press, Peng De, Vice President of the American Chamber of Commerce of California, has extensive experience in engineering. Recently, he and his wife have been traveling around the world. On Sunday (the 20th), they arrived in Shanghai from Pinghan. According to an interview with a reporter from the Continental Press, the general American public knows very little about Chinese customs, culture, and history. If this understanding can be developed, it will greatly increase the happiness of the Pacific region. This trip is his first time in China and he cannot stay long, but the unlimited potential for China's future development cannot help but move him. China has a large population and abundant resources, which makes it very promising. The most important thing is to build roads to facilitate transportation and unify the language. One thing that is surprising is that China still uses traditional methods to manage new-era construction projects. For example, a dam can be completed in one year using modern methods, but it takes five years using traditional methods. Is China's inability to achieve real progress due to adhering to old ways in all matters? According to Peng and his wife, they left Los Angeles on March 19th and spent several weeks traveling in Japan, Korea, and North China. According to Peng, there is no doubt that Korea has made progress, but Koreans are still openly opposed to Japan.
